If you have a problem with his LACK OF PREPARATION.. And you supposedly "LOVE HIM LIKE A BROTHER!!" Then you just talk to him privately and, ask for him to pull his weight.. With that said, I don't know how DC's LACK OF Film Study, affects their partnership behind the scenes.. But as a SUPER HARDCORE UFC and Pro Wrestling along with bigger Boxing Fights Student I am.. I pay A LOT MORE ATTENTION than I should on commentary teams, play-by-play talent, color commentators, and analysts.. I look for chemistry and all of that.. Too me, DC is more of a NATURAL at the job.. He has intangibles on commentary, that YOU WILL NOT TEACH OR WILL HAVE TO WORK SO HARD AT IT, THAT IT WILL NOT COME ACROSS AS NATURAL!! For what his role is on commentary, he does it AWESOME!! Now usually that NATURAL ABILITY comes with a LACK OF PREPARATION!! Because your so effortlessly good at it, that you may not work as hard at it.. DC has a certain commentary-friendly charisma that Cruz will never have, no matter how much he tries.. I like Cruz on commentary better now than when he started but, you can also tell he has to work harder to not make the mistakes he makes.. DC is more of a SOUNDBYTES Style color commentator.. Cruz is more of an analyst.. Cruz would actually serve better on the desk, in my opinion.. He is more in-depth, so therefore I find that he over steps on commentary, doesn't know how to GET IN and GET OUT with his commentary, gets to rambling on at times too.. He's well-spoken, very smart, and thinks outside the box as opposed to keeping with a GENERAL OUTLINE!! Those are strong points, but as you see in this interview, he tends to OVER-TALK, and sometimes his message (even though smart and from a different view) comes off pretentious and somewhat condescending, which is not good in commentary.. DC while using a more GENERAL OUTLINE, and the amazing relatable charisma he has, along with a GENUINE EXCITEMENT, keeps it simple but, relatable to a casual fan.. I'm all for ACCOUNTABILITY but, I do believe Cruz could of handled it more professionally, but at the end of the day, as long as they can talk it over, work together (which it obviously looks like they can), it's really NO BIG DEAL!!

Both of these guys have potential to be quality on the mic.  Just need to stay away from the 3 big problems plaguing commentary.   1) Trying to be judges.  The fans can do that themselves, and stick to breaking down the fights.  I adore when they go into technique breakdowns or identify specifically what the fighters are looking for in their movements.  Anyways, unless rounds are stupidly obvious, they should stray away from it.  2) Trying to justify early stoppages.  Fighters get rocked all the time, just because their hurt doesn't mean its over, even with the potential to be.  A fight can still be stopped too early.  3) Talking about striking numbers.  Not all strikes are made equal.  Its like shots on goal in hockey.  It might often point to the winner, but is never a metric to glue yourself to compared to what your eyes are seeing.  Especially when live numbers are inaccurate.
